padding-right:0.5em;"><a href="/wiki/List_of_language_regulators" title="List of language regulators">Regulated&#160;by</a></th><td style="line-height:1.35em;"><b>Portugal</b>:<br /><a href="/wiki/Lisbon_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Lisbon Academy of Sciences">Lisbon Academy of Sciences</a> <small>(<a href="/wiki/Lisbon_Academy_of_Sciences,_Class_of_Letters" title="Lisbon Academy of Sciences, Class of Letters">Lisbon Academy Class of Letters</a>)</small> <br /> <b>Brazil</b>:<br /> <a href="/wiki/Academia_Brasileira_de_Letras" title="Academia Brasileira de Letras">Academia Brasileira de Letras</a></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;color: black; background-color:  #c9ffd9;">Language codes</th></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-top:0.225em;line-height:1.1em; padding-right:0.5em;"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/ISO_639-1" title="ISO 639-1">ISO 639-1</a></span></th><td style="line-height:1.35em;"><code><span class="plainlinks"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.loc.gov/standards/iso639-2/php/langcodes_name.php?iso_639_1=pt">pt</a></span></code></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-top:0.225em;line-height:1.1em; padding-right:0.5em;"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/ISO_639-2" title="ISO 639-2">ISO 639-2</a></span></th><td style="line-height:1.35em;"><code><span class="plainlinks"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.loc.gov/standards/iso639-2/php/langcodes_name.php?code_ID=363">por</a></span></code></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-top:0.225em;line-height:1.1em; padding-right:0.5em;"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/ISO_639-3" title="ISO 639-3">ISO 639-3</a></span></th><td style="line-height:1.35em;"><code><a href="https://iso639-3.sil.org/code/por" class="extiw" title="iso639-3:por">por</a></code></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-top:0.225em;line-height:1.1em; padding-right:0.5em;"><a href="/wiki/Glottolog" title="Glottolog">Glottolog</a></th><td style="line-height:1.35em;"><code><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://glottolog.org/resource/languoid/id/port1283">port1283</a></code><sup id="cite_ref-Glottolog_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Glottolog-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-top:0.225em;line-height:1.1em; padding-right:0.5em;"><a href="/wiki/Linguasphere_Observatory" title="Linguasphere Observatory">Linguasphere</a></th><td style="line-height:1.35em;"><code>51-AAA-a</code></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height:1.35em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_the_portuguese_language_in_the_world.svg" class="image"><img alt="Map of the portuguese language in the world.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Map_of_the_portuguese_language_in_the_world.svg/220px-Map_of_the_portuguese_language_in_the_world.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="97" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Map_of_the_portuguese_language_in_the_world.svg/330px-Map_of_the_portuguese_language_in_the_world.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Map_of_the_portuguese_language_in_the_world.svg/440px-Map_of_the_portuguese_language_in_the_world.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1498" data-file-height="660" /></a><div style="text-align:left;"><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #015A01; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Native language</div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #339900; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Official and administrative language</div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #98FC66; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Cultural or secondary language</div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #00FF00; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Portuguese-speaking minorities</div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FFFF40; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Portuguese-based_creole_languages" title="Portuguese-based creole languages">Portuguese-based creole languages</a></div></div>
</td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="noprint selfref" style="text-align:center;background-color:#ddddff;padding:0.3em 0.5em;text-align:left;line-height:1.3;"><b>This article contains <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">IPA</a> phonetic symbols.</b> Without proper <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA#Rendering_issues" title="Help:IPA">rendering support</a>, you may see <a href="/wiki/Replacement_character" class="mw-redirect" title="Replacement character">question marks, boxes, or other symbols</a> instead of <a href="/wiki/Unicode" title="Unicode">Unicode</a> characters. For an introductory guide on IPA symbols, see <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">Help:IPA</a>.</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Portuguese</b> (<i lang="pt" title="Portuguese language text">português</i> or, in full, <i lang="pt" title="Portuguese language text">língua portuguesa</i>) is a <a href="/wiki/Western_Romance_languages" title="Western Romance languages">Western Romance language</a> originating in the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a>. It is the sole official language of <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">Cape Verde</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau" title="Guinea-Bissau">Guinea-Bissau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a>, <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a> and <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="São Tomé and Príncipe">São Tomé and Príncipe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CPLP_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPLP-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> It also has co-official language status in <a href="/wiki/East_Timor" title="East Timor">East Timor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea" title="Equatorial Guinea">Equatorial Guinea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a> in China. As the result of expansion during colonial times, a cultural presence of Portuguese and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese-based_creole_languages" title="Portuguese-based creole languages">Portuguese creole</a> speakers are also found in <a href="/wiki/Goa" title="Goa">Goa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Daman_and_Diu" title="Daman and Diu">Daman and Diu</a> in India;<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Batticaloa" title="Batticaloa">Batticaloa</a> on the east coast of <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a>; in the <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesian</a> island of <a href="/wiki/Flores" title="Flores">Flores</a>; in the <a href="/wiki/Malacca" title="Malacca">Malacca</a> state of <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>; and the <a href="/wiki/ABC_islands_(Lesser_Antilles)" title="ABC islands (Lesser Antilles)">ABC islands</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> where <a href="/wiki/Papiamento" title="Papiamento">Papiamento</a> is spoken, while <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verdean_Creole" title="Cape Verdean Creole">Cape Verdean Creole</a> is the most widely spoken Portuguese-based Creole.  A Portuguese-speaking person or nation is referred to as "<a href="/wiki/Lusophone" title="Lusophone">Lusophone</a>" (<i>Lusófono</i>).
</p><p>Portuguese is part of the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Romance_languages" title="Iberian Romance languages">Ibero-Romance group</a> that evolved from several dialects of <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">Vulgar Latin</a> in the medieval <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Galicia" title="Kingdom of Galicia">Kingdom of Galicia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/County_of_Portugal" title="County of Portugal">County of Portugal</a>, and has kept some <a href="/wiki/Gallaecian_language" title="Gallaecian language">Celtic</a> phonology and lexicon.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> With approximately 215 to 220 million native speakers and 250 million total speakers, Portuguese is usually listed as the sixth <a href="/wiki/List_of_languages_by_number_of_native_speakers" title="List of languages by number of native speakers">most natively spoken language</a> in the world, the third-most spoken European language in the world in terms of native speakers,<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> and the most spoken language in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere" title="Southern Hemisphere">Southern Hemisphere</a>. It is also the second-most spoken language, after <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>, in <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a> and all of <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>, and is one of the 10 most spoken languages in <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> and is an official language of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mercosur" title="Mercosur">Mercosur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States#Official_languages" title="Organization of American States">OAS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economic_Community_of_West_African_States" title="Economic Community of West African States">ECOWAS</a> and the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">Community of Portuguese Language Countries</a> is an international organization made up of all of the world's officially Lusophone nations.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Portuguese_language" class="mw-redirect" title="History of the Portuguese language">History of the Portuguese language</a></div>
<p>When the Romans arrived at the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a> in 216&#160;BC, they brought the <a href="/wiki/Latin_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin language">Latin language</a> with them, from which all Romance languages descend. The language was spread by Roman soldiers, settlers, and merchants, who built <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Roman</a> cities mostly near the settlements of previous <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celtic</a> or <a href="/wiki/Celtiberians" title="Celtiberians">Celtiberian</a> civilizations established long before the Roman arrivals. For that reason, the language has kept a relevant substratum of much older, <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Europe" title="Atlantic Europe">Atlantic European</a> <a href="/wiki/Megalithic_Culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Megalithic Culture">Megalithic Culture</a><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celtic culture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Between AD 409 and AD 711, as the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> collapsed in <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western Europe</a>, the Iberian Peninsula was conquered by <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic peoples</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Migration_Period" title="Migration Period">Migration Period</a>. The occupiers, mainly <a href="/wiki/Suebi" title="Suebi">Suebi</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Visigoths" title="Visigoths">Visigoths</a> and <a href="/wiki/Buri_tribe" title="Buri tribe">Buri</a><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> who originally spoke <a href="/wiki/Germanic_languages" title="Germanic languages">Germanic languages</a>, quickly adopted late Roman culture and the <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">Vulgar Latin</a> dialects of the peninsula and over the next 300 years totally integrated into the local populations. After the <a href="/wiki/Moors" title="Moors">Moorish</a> invasion beginning in 711, <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a> became the administrative and common language in the conquered regions, but most of the <a href="/wiki/Mozarabs" title="Mozarabs">remaining Christian population</a> continued to speak a form of <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">Romance</a> commonly known as <a href="/wiki/Mozarabic_language" title="Mozarabic language">Mozarabic</a>, which lasted three centuries longer in <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>. Like other Neo-Latin and European languages, Portuguese has adopted a significant number of <a href="/wiki/Loanword" title="Loanword">loanwords</a> from <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> mainly for technical and scientific terminology. These borrowings occurred via Latin, and later during the Middle Ages and the Renaissance.
</p><p>Portuguese evolved from the medieval language, known today by linguists as <a href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese" title="Galician-Portuguese">Galician-Portuguese</a>, Old Portuguese or Old Galician, of the northwestern medieval <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Galicia" title="Kingdom of Galicia">Kingdom of Galicia</a> and <a href="/wiki/County_of_Portugal" title="County of Portugal">County of Portugal</a>. It is in Latin administrative documents of the 9th century that written Galician-Portuguese words and phrases are first recorded. This phase is known as Proto-Portuguese, which lasted from the 9th century until the 12th-century independence of the <a href="/wiki/County_of_Portugal" title="County of Portugal">County of Portugal</a> from the Kingdom of León, which had by then assumed reign over Galicia.
</p><p>In the first part of the <a href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese" title="Galician-Portuguese">Galician-Portuguese</a> period (from the 12th to the 14th century), the language was increasingly used for documents and other written forms. For some time, it was the language of preference for <a href="/wiki/Lyric_poetry" title="Lyric poetry">lyric poetry</a> in Christian <a href="/wiki/Hispania" title="Hispania">Hispania</a>, much as <a href="/wiki/Occitan" class="mw-redirect" title="Occitan">Occitan</a> was the language of the <a href="/wiki/Occitan_literature#Poetry_of_the_troubadours" title="Occitan literature">poetry of the troubadours</a> in France. The Occitan digraphs <i>lh</i> and <i>nh</i>, used in its classical orthography, were adopted by the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_alphabet#Basic_digraphs" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese alphabet">orthography of Portuguese</a>, presumably by <a href="/wiki/Gerald_of_Braga" title="Gerald of Braga">Gerald of Braga</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> a monk from <a href="/wiki/Moissac" title="Moissac">Moissac</a>, who became bishop of <a href="/wiki/Braga" title="Braga">Braga</a> in Portugal in 1047, playing a major role in modernizing written Portuguese using classical <a href="/wiki/Occitan_language" title="Occitan language">Occitan</a> norms.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Portugal became an independent kingdom in 1139, under King <a href="/wiki/Afonso_I_of_Portugal" title="Afonso I of Portugal">Afonso I of Portugal</a>. In 1290, King <a href="/wiki/Denis_of_Portugal" title="Denis of Portugal">Denis of Portugal</a> created the first Portuguese university in Lisbon (the <i>Estudos Gerais</i>, which later moved to <a href="/wiki/University_of_Coimbra" title="University of Coimbra">Coimbra</a>) and decreed for Portuguese, then simply called the "common language", to be known as the Portuguese language and used officially.
</p><p>In the second period of Old Portuguese, in the 15th and 16th centuries, with the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">Portuguese discoveries</a>, the language was taken to many regions of Africa, Asia, and the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>. By the mid-16th century, Portuguese had become a <i><a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a></i> in Asia and Africa, used not only for colonial administration and trade but also for communication between local officials and Europeans of all nationalities.
</p><p>Its spread was helped by mixed marriages between Portuguese and local people and by its association with <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholic</a> <a href="/wiki/Missionary" title="Missionary">missionary</a> efforts, which led to the formation of <a href="/wiki/Creole_language" title="Creole language">creole languages</a> such as that called <a href="/wiki/Kristang_language" title="Kristang language">Kristang</a> in many parts of Asia (from the word <i>cristão</i>, "Christian"). The language continued to be popular in parts of Asia until the 19th century. Some Portuguese-speaking Christian communities in <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> preserved their language even after they were isolated from Portugal.
</p><p>The end of the Old Portuguese period was marked by the publication of the <i>Cancioneiro Geral</i> by <a href="/wiki/Garcia_de_Resende" title="Garcia de Resende">Garcia de Resende</a>, in 1516. The early times of Modern Portuguese, which spans the period from the 16th century to the present day, were characterized by an increase in the number of learned words borrowed from <a href="/wiki/Classical_Latin" title="Classical Latin">Classical Latin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">Classical Greek</a> because of the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a> (learned words borrowed from Latin also came from <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_Latin" title="Renaissance Latin">Renaissance Latin</a>, the form of Latin during that time), which greatly enriched the lexicon. Most literate Portuguese speakers were also literate in Latin; and thus they easily adopted Latin words into their writing&#160;– and eventually speech&#160;– in Portuguese.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Spanish author <a href="/wiki/Miguel_de_Cervantes" title="Miguel de Cervantes">Miguel de Cervantes</a> once called Portuguese "the sweet and gracious language", while the Brazilian poet <a href="/wiki/Olavo_Bilac" title="Olavo Bilac">Olavo Bilac</a> described it as <i lang="pt" title="Portuguese language text">a última flor do Lácio, inculta e bela</i> ("the last flower of <a href="/wiki/Latium" title="Latium">Latium</a>, rustic and beautiful"). Portuguese is also termed "the language of Camões", after <a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%ADs_Vaz_de_Cam%C3%B5es" class="mw-redirect" title="Luís Vaz de Camões">Luís Vaz de Camões</a>, one of the greatest literary figures in the Portuguese language and author of the Portuguese <a href="/wiki/Epic_poem" class="mw-redirect" title="Epic poem">epic poem</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Os_Lus%C3%ADadas" title="Os Lusíadas">Os Lusíadas</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2006, the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_the_Portuguese_Language" title="Museum of the Portuguese Language">Museum of the Portuguese Language</a>, an interactive museum about the Portuguese language, was founded in <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="São Paulo">São Paulo</a>, Brazil, the city with the greatest number of Portuguese language speakers in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-NOVA_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NOVA-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The museum is the first of its kind in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-NOVA_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NOVA-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> In 2015 the museum was destroyed in a fire, but there are plans to reconstruct it.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<td align="right">216,226
</td></tr>

</th></tr></tbody></table>
<table class="box-Cleanup plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style ambox-Cleanup" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/40px-Edit-clear.svg.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/60px-Edit-clear.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/80px-Edit-clear.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="48" data-file-height="48" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section may <b>require <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Cleanup" title="Wikipedia:Cleanup">cleanup</a></b> to meet Wikipedia's <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style">quality standards</a>. The specific problem is: <b>Hard to navigate due to the amount of tables.</b><span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_language&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> if you can.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">July 2019</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Multilingual_Emergency_Assembly_Area_Sign_in_Oizumi.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Multilingual_Emergency_Assembly_Area_Sign_in_Oizumi.JPG/220px-Multilingual_Emergency_Assembly_Area_Sign_in_Oizumi.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Multilingual_Emergency_Assembly_Area_Sign_in_Oizumi.JPG/330px-Multilingual_Emergency_Assembly_Area_Sign_in_Oizumi.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Multilingual_Emergency_Assembly_Area_Sign_in_Oizumi.JPG/440px-Multilingual_Emergency_Assembly_Area_Sign_in_Oizumi.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Multilingual_Emergency_Assembly_Area_Sign_in_Oizumi.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Multilingual sign in Japanese, Chinese, Portuguese, and English in <a href="/wiki/Oizumi" class="mw-redirect" title="Oizumi">Oizumi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>. Return immigration of <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Brazilians" title="Japanese Brazilians">Japanese Brazilians</a> has led to a large Portuguese-speaking community in the town.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Portuguese is the native language of the vast majority of people in Brazil<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> and Portugal,<sup id="cite_ref-Special_Eurobarometer_243_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Special_Eurobarometer_243-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Perhaps 75% of the population of urban Angola speaks Portuguese natively,<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> while approximately 85% fluent; these rates are significantly lower in the countryside.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Just over 40% (and rapidly increasing) of the population of Mozambique are native speakers of Portuguese, and 60% are fluent, according to the 2007 census.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Portuguese is also spoken natively by 30% of the population in Guinea-Bissau, and a Portuguese-based creole is understood by all.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> No data is available for Cape Verde, but almost all the population is bilingual, and the monolingual population speaks the Portuguese-based <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verdean_Creole" title="Cape Verdean Creole">Cape Verdean Creole</a>.  Portuguese is mentioned in the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_South_Africa" title="Constitution of South Africa">Constitution of South Africa</a> as one of the languages spoken by communities within the country for which the <a href="/wiki/Pan_South_African_Language_Board" title="Pan South African Language Board">Pan South African Language Board</a> was charged with promoting and ensuring respect.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are also significant Portuguese-speaking immigrant communities in many countries including <a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">Andorra</a> (15.4%),<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> (400,275 people in the 2006 census),<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> (900,000 people),<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> (400,000 people),<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jersey" title="Jersey">Jersey</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">Namibia</a> (about 4–5% of the population, mainly refugees from Angola in the north of the country),<sup id="cite_ref-www.namibian.com.na_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www.namibian.com.na-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Paraguay" title="Paraguay">Paraguay</a> (10.7% or 636,000 people),<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a> (0.6% or 12,000 people),<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a> (196,000 nationals in 2008),<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a> (554,000).<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> and the United States (0.35% of the population or 1,228,126 speakers according to the 2007 <a href="/wiki/American_Community_Survey" title="American Community Survey">American Community Survey</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In some parts of former <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_India" title="Portuguese India">Portuguese India</a>, namely <a href="/wiki/Goa" title="Goa">Goa</a><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Daman_and_Diu" title="Daman and Diu">Daman and Diu</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> the language is still spoken by about 10,000 people. In 2014, an estimated 1,500 students were learning Portuguese in Goa.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Official_status">Official status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Official status">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_territorial_entities_where_Portuguese_is_an_official_language" title="List of territorial entities where Portuguese is an official language">List of territorial entities where Portuguese is an official language</a></div>
<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lusophone_World.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Lusophone_World.svg/220px-Lusophone_World.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="97" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Lusophone_World.svg/330px-Lusophone_World.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Lusophone_World.svg/440px-Lusophone_World.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="940" data-file-height="415" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lusophone_World.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Countries and regions where Portuguese has official status.</div></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">Community of Portuguese Language Countries</a><sup id="cite_ref-CPLP_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPLP-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
(in Portuguese <i>Comunidade dos Países de Língua Portuguesa</i>, with the Portuguese acronym CPLP) consists of the eight independent countries that have Portuguese as an <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a>: <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">Cape Verde</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Timor" title="East Timor">East Timor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea" title="Equatorial Guinea">Equatorial Guinea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau" title="Guinea-Bissau">Guinea-Bissau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> and <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="São Tomé and Príncipe">São Tomé and Príncipe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CPLP_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPLP-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea" title="Equatorial Guinea">Equatorial Guinea</a> made a formal application for full membership to the CPLP in June 2010, a status given only to states with Portuguese as an official language.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, Portuguese became its third official language (besides <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> and, in July 2014, the country was accepted as a member of the CPLP.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Portuguese is also one of the official languages of the Special Administrative Region of the People's Republic of China of Macau (alongside <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>) and of several international organizations, including <a href="/wiki/Mercosur" title="Mercosur">Mercosur</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_Ibero-American_States" title="Organization of Ibero-American States">Organization of Ibero-American States</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_South_American_Nations" title="Union of South American Nations">Union of South American Nations</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">Organization of American States</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-africa-union.org_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-africa-union.org-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Economic_Community_of_West_African_States" title="Economic Community of West African States">Economic Community of West African States</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-africa-union.org_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-africa-union.org-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community" title="Southern African Development Community">Southern African Development Community</a><sup id="cite_ref-africa-union.org_57-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-africa-union.org-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lusophone_countries">Lusophone countries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Lusophone countries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<td colspan="3"><a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">Community of Portuguese Language Countries</a>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><small>Notes:
</small></p><small></small><ol><small><li><a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a> is not a sovereign nation. It is one of the two semi-autonomous <a href="/wiki/Special_Administrative_Region_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Special Administrative Region of the People&#39;s Republic of China">Special Administrative Regions of the People's Republic of China</a> (the other being <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">Anglophone</a> <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>, a former <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">British</a> colony).</li>
</small><li><small><a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea" title="Equatorial Guinea">Equatorial Guinea</a> adopted Portuguese as one of its official languages in 2007, being admitted to CPLP in 2014. The use of the Portuguese language in this country is limited. However, a Portuguese-based creole language, <a href="/wiki/Annobonese_Creole" title="Annobonese Creole">Annobonese Creole</a>, is used, mainly on the islands of <a href="/wiki/Annobon" class="mw-redirect" title="Annobon">Annobon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bioko" title="Bioko">Bioko</a>.</small></li></ol>
<p>The combined population of the entire <a href="/wiki/Lusophone" title="Lusophone">Lusophone</a> area was estimated at 279 million in July 2017. This number does not include the Lusophone <a href="/wiki/Diaspora" title="Diaspora">diaspora</a>, estimated at approximately 10 million people (including 4.5 million Portuguese, 3 million Brazilians, and half a million Cape Verdeans, among others), although it is hard to obtain official accurate numbers of diasporic Portuguese speakers because a significant portion of these citizens are naturalized citizens born outside of Lusophone territory or are children of immigrants, and may have only a basic command of the language. Additionally, a large part of the diaspora is a part of the already-counted population of the Portuguese-speaking countries and territories, such as the high number of Brazilian and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese-speaking_African_countries" title="Portuguese-speaking African countries">PALOP</a> emigrant citizens in Portugal or the high number of Portuguese emigrant citizens in the PALOP and Brazil.
</p><p>The Portuguese language therefore serves more than 250 million people daily, who have direct or indirect legal, juridical and social contact with it, varying from the only language used in any contact, to only education, contact with local or international administration, commerce and services or the simple sight of road signs, public information and advertising in Portuguese.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Portuguese_as_a_foreign_language">Portuguese as a foreign language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Portuguese as a foreign language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Portuguese is a mandatory subject in the school curriculum in <a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">Uruguay</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Other countries where Portuguese is commonly taught in schools or where it has been introduced as an option include <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">Republic of the Congo</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-estadao_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-estadao-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-estadao_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-estadao-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">Namibia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-www.namibian.com.na_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www.namibian.com.na-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Eswatini" title="Eswatini">Eswatini (Swaziland)</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-estadao_63-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-estadao-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-estadao_63-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-estadao-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast" title="Ivory Coast">Ivory Coast</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>. In 2017, a project was launched in order to introduce Portuguese as a school subject in <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a> too.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Also, according to Portugal's Minister of Foreign Affairs, the language will be part of the school curriculum of 32 countries in total by 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> In the countries listed below Portuguese is spoken either as native language by minorities due to the Portuguese colonial past or as a <i><a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a></i> in bordering and multilingual regions, such as on the border between Brazil and Uruguay and Angola and Namibia.
</p>
